## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Common models include nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and external/parametric forcing terms that depend on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped, unforced) oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple Hooke-type restoring acceleration, sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type damping at higher Reynolds number)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sign(v) (velocity-opposing friction with nearly constant magnitude)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity plus damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order conservative stiffness nonlinearity)
- Simple pendulum (exact restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (periodic restoring torque for large-angle oscillations, with damping)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (harmonic forcing at frequency c3)
- Multi-tone / general periodic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (richer external drive)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-periodic modulation of stiffness)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited Liénard form): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x| → limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excitation via velocity-dependent damping)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic viscous): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (damping force increasing strongly with speed, or effective nonlinear dissipation)
- Conservative potential-gradient form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (dv_dt as minus derivative of a polynomial potential U(x))
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * x**2) * x + c2 * v (effective stiffness depends on amplitude, common in weakly nonlinear oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: odd functions of x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)) typically indicate center-symmetric springs/potentials; even-power terms often imply symmetry breaking or bias forces.
- Conservative vs dissipative split: terms depending only on x correspond to potential forces; terms proportional to v (or functions of v) correspond to dissipation/energy injection.
- Dry friction signature: a sign(v) term produces piecewise-constant acceleration offsets and can create stick–slip or non-smooth trajectories near v ≈ 0.
- Quadratic drag signature: v*Abs(v) yields stronger damping at high speed and asymmetric phase-portrait curvature compared to linear damping.
- Limit-cycle generation: negative linear damping near the origin combined with positive nonlinear damping (e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v) produces self-sustained oscillations with amplitude regulation.
- Hardening/softening identification: +x**3 (with appropriate sign) leads to amplitude-dependent frequency shifts (hardening or softening Duffing behavior) observable as bent resonance curves under forcing.
- Time-periodic coefficients: factors like (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x indicate parametric resonance regions (Mathieu instability tongues) rather than simple forced resonance.
- External drive markers: additive sin/cos(t) terms imply energy input at specific frequencies; the response often shows phase-locking and resonance peaks.
- Non-smooth vs smooth dynamics: Abs(v) or sign(v) introduces non-differentiability that often manifests as corners in phase portraits and may require piecewise modeling in regression.

Note: `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, so `cos(c*t + c)` can match `sin(t)` if c2=1, c3=-π/2.

**Key question for each candidate:** Can the candidate's terms be reduced to exactly {v³, x·|v|^(1/3), x, sin(t)}?

**The critical term is `x*|v|^(1/3)`.** Let me check which candidates have a term that can represent this.

**Candidates with `x*log(c*|v|+1)` terms (1,2,3,4,5,6,7,8,15,16,17,18,19,20,21):** `log(c*|v|+1)` is NOT equivalent to `|v|^(1/3)`. These are fundamentally different functions - logarithm vs power function. **[NO MATCH]** for all of these unless they have other terms that could work.

**Candidates with `v^c * x` terms (9,10,11,12,13,14):** `|v|^c * x` where c can be set to 1/3. But `v^c` is NOT `|v|^c` when v can be negative. However, looking at candidate 13: `c6*v**c7*x` — for v negative and c7=1/3, `v^(1/3)` is the real cube root (negative), while `|v|^(1/3)` is positive. These differ in sign for negative v. **[NO MATCH]** for these.

**Candidates with `cos(t)*|v|^c` terms (23,25,26,27,28):** These couple |v| with cos(t), not with x. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates with `v*|v|` terms (15-20, 37,38,45-48):** `v*|v| = |v|*v = sign(v)*v²`. This is NOT `v³`. Actually, `v³ = v*v² = v*|v|²`... no. But `v*|v|` is NOT `v³`. These are different functions. **[NO MATCH]** for the v³ term replacement. However, some also have explicit v terms. `c1*v + c2*v*|v|` cannot equal `c*v³` for all v. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates with only `x*cos(t)` coupling (31,33-36,43,44):** These have `x*cos(c*t)` which couples x and t. The GT has no x-t coupling. Setting c5=0 eliminates this term, but then we lose the ability to represent `x*|v|^(1/3)`. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates 49,50:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2*t+c3) + c4*v³ + c5*sin/cos(c6*t+c7)`. These have x, v³, and two trig terms in t, but NO `x*|v|^(1/3)` term. **[NO MATCH]**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the basis function `x*|v|^(1/3)` (or any equivalent). The log-based candidates use `log(|v|)` which is fundamentally different, and the power-based candidates use `v^c` (not `|v|^c`), which differs for negative v.

Let me verify all candidates systematically — none have `x*|v|^(c)` with proper absolute value handling that could match `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.

Matched candidate IDs: []

[NO MATCH]
